  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_19218d35-32c8-4bfe-9105-2a65e8797c42'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15203016379486639746">#1 <i>New York Times</i>-bestselling author Nora Roberts explores the wilds of the Grand Tetons-and the mysteries of love, murder, and madness-in her engrossing and passionate new novel.<br/><br/>Reece Gilmore has come a long way to see the stunning view below her. As the sole survivor of a brutal crime back East, she has been on the run, desperately fighting the nightmares and panic attac</span>
  <span id="freeText15203016379486639746" style="display:none">#1 <i>New York Times</i>-bestselling author Nora Roberts explores the wilds of the Grand Tetons-and the mysteries of love, murder, and madness-in her engrossing and passionate new novel.<br /><br />Reece Gilmore has come a long way to see the stunning view below her. As the sole survivor of a brutal crime back East, she has been on the run, desperately fighting the nightmares and panic attacks that haunt her. Reece settles in Angel's Fist, Wyoming-temporarily, at least-and takes a job at a local diner. And now she's hiked this mountain all by herself. It was glorious, she thought, as she peered through her binoculars at the Snake River churning below.<br /><br />Then Reece saw the man and woman on the opposite bank. Arguing. Fighting. And suddenly, the man was on top of the woman, his hands around her throat . . .<br /><br />Enjoying a moment of solitude a bit farther down the trail is a gruff loner named Brody. But by the time Reece reaches him and brings him to the scene, the pair has vanished. When authorities comb the area where she saw the attack, they find nothing. No signs of struggle. No freshly turned earth. Not even a tire track.<br /><br />And no one in Angel's Fist seems to believe her. After all, she's a newcomer in town, with a reputation for being jumpy and jittery-maybe even a little fragile. Maybe it's time to run again, to move on . . .<br /><br />Reece Gilmore knows there's a killer in Angel's Fist, even if Brody, despite his seeming impatience and desire to keep her at arm's length, is the only one willing to believe her. When a series of menacing events makes it clear that someone wants her out of the way, Reece must put her trust in Brody-and herself-to find out if there is a killer in Angel's Fist before it's too late.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15203016379486639746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11243357564628380536"><b>Somewhere between 3 and 4 stars</b><br/><br/>Quite enjoyable. Heavier on romance than on suspense for most of the book.<br/><br/>Loved the small-town setting with all its quirks and follies though I wasn't too invested in the characters.<br/><br/>The heroine was annoying as hell but she grew some backbone eventually and thankfully didn't ruin too much of the book for me. The hero was likable enough.<br/><br/>The story was interesting but the mystery was a bit weak. I guessed the killer right from the beginning. The author gave him too muc</span>
  <span id="freeText11243357564628380536" style="display:none"><b>Somewhere between 3 and 4 stars</b><br /><br />Quite enjoyable. Heavier on romance than on suspense for most of the book.<br /><br />Loved the small-town setting with all its quirks and follies though I wasn't too invested in the characters.<br /><br />The heroine was annoying as hell but she grew some backbone eventually and thankfully didn't ruin too much of the book for me. The hero was likable enough.<br /><br />The story was interesting but the mystery was a bit weak. I guessed the killer right from the beginning. The author gave him too much attention in my opinion.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2013183271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2013183271" />
    <a title="Fareya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22583912-fareya"><img alt="Fareya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485406498p2/22583912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2013183271?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fareya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fareya" href="/user/show/22583912-fareya">Fareya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013183271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2979973153169085458">Sometimes, when I can't decide what to read next, I just pick up one of Nora Roberts' romantic suspense novels and I am never disappointed. Nora sure knows how to leave her readers satisfied. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26050.Angels_Fall' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angels Fall</a> is one of those exceptionally well written, engaging NR style thriller with just the right pace, fast enough to keep one interested, but taking its time to build up the plot and characters. <br/><br/>Based in a picturesque little town at the foot of the Grand Tetons, the story revolves around Reece Gilmor</span>
  <span id="freeText2979973153169085458" style="display:none">Sometimes, when I can't decide what to read next, I just pick up one of Nora Roberts' romantic suspense novels and I am never disappointed. Nora sure knows how to leave her readers satisfied. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26050.Angels_Fall" rel="nofollow noopener">Angels Fall</a> is one of those exceptionally well written, engaging NR style thriller with just the right pace, fast enough to keep one interested, but taking its time to build up the plot and characters. <br /><br />Based in a picturesque little town at the foot of the Grand Tetons, the story revolves around Reece Gilmore, a survivor from Boston. Desperately trying to cope up with the after shocks of a traumatic event, Reece has been on the road for a while. One day she stumbles in a small Wyoming town. Charmed by the majestic mountains surrounding it and the fresh, crisp air she decides to stay for sometime. She takes up the job of a cook at a local diner and works towards getting on with her life.<br /><br />One day while hiking on a mountain trail, she witnesses a man strangling a woman down by the river. Reece reports the crime, but when the authorities investigate, they find nothing. No signs of struggle, no trace that anyone was even there. As she is a newcomer, emotionally fragile with a reputation of being skittish, nobody in town believes her, except for a reclusive loner and writer, Brody.<br /><br />Its an engrossing mystery-romance. The character development is remarkable. Reece, even though vulnerable and and a bit paranoid, manages to hold her ground and works on getting stronger, more confident and is also making friends in town. The way she coped by keeping a clear head for the most part with all the mind games that the killer was playing on her was impressive. Brody, even though some what pushy was exactly what Reece needed. Beneath his hard exterior and grumpiness he is a kind and caring person. The chemistry between Reece and Brody was amazing and very believable which is usually not the case in most romance stories. <br /><br />With entertaining secondary characters, witty dialogues, small town drama and a murder involved, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26050.Angels_Fall" rel="nofollow noopener">Angels Fall</a> is a captivating read. The lush descriptions of the mountains, the lake and the natural scenery in general was like a virtual brief vacation in the Grand Tetons. Overall a solid romantic suspense novel and a satisfying read. Nothing less than what I expect out of a Nora Roberts book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2979973153169085458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2363508280" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2363508280" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424631975p2/2490110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2363508280?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2018</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=contemporary-mystery">contemporary-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=my-kindle">my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=small-town">small-town</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2363508280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9786518838415955538">Not bad, but also not good either.<br/><br/>I mean, there are good parts, but they’re offset by little things I find annoying and there were a lot of these little things which accumulated at the end. So it was a bumpy read. The Montana setting and vivid descriptions of a small town sitting at the foot of the Grand Tetons were a nice touch though, and the main character was sympathetic. Easily my favorite part of the whole book was the setting. Everything else was mostly filler.<br/><br/>A couple of weeks ago my nei</span>
  <span id="freeText9786518838415955538" style="display:none">Not bad, but also not good either.<br /><br />I mean, there are good parts, but they’re offset by little things I find annoying and there were a lot of these little things which accumulated at the end. So it was a bumpy read. The Montana setting and vivid descriptions of a small town sitting at the foot of the Grand Tetons were a nice touch though, and the main character was sympathetic. Easily my favorite part of the whole book was the setting. Everything else was mostly filler.<br /><br />A couple of weeks ago my neighbor got a new job out of state and I “inherited” her library. Normally this would be exciting–I love sorting through books–but this time, not so much. She and I don’t have much in common book-wise, and her collection consists of fiction, lots of mysteries and thrillers and quite a few romances. All contemporaries and not a single sci-fi or fantasy in the bunch. All huge door-stoppers too. Majority of these will go to charity because I have my own pile of similar fiction that I still haven’t been able to chip at no matter how much I avoid it try.<br /><br />Anyhow. I now have a huge stash of Nora Roberts books and it’s been a real–chore?–experience sorting through them.<br /><br />I went into this book expecting–well, hoping–it’s like The Witness which was a pleasant surprise and I enjoyed it more than I thought I would. This book has a similar set-up: small town, picturesque backdrop, lots of wilderness, nosy busy-body townsfolk, protagonist with a traumatic past who is on her own, and a murder mystery plot in the background. What’s different from The Witness is the uneven pacing and utterly unlikable love interest who is actually quite an ass. This turned out to be the sticking point with me because I could not get over how much of an ass he was. Moreover, I could not see what she saw in him, and so I couldn’t get into the story whenever he appeared, being all ass-like.<br /><br />More on this book in particular when I get home.<br /><br />* * * * * <br /><br />I’m home now, but still don’t have much to say about this book. Maybe with a little more time it’ll come to me. For now though, all I can say is this book makes me angry, and not in a good way, because the set-up is good and there is so much potential for the rest of the book to be good. But unfortunately Nora Roberts had to go and be all Nora Roberts all over the damn book. I wouldn’t say she ruined it, because I’ve read worse, but she got very close. So much potential, all wasted.<br /><br />*angry muttering*<br /><br />It could have been SO GOOD.<br /><br />Originally posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2018/07/15/angels-fall-by-nora-roberts/">https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9786518838415955538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_488499730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488499730" />
    <a title="SB*needs low angst books*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8385892-sb-needs-low-angst-books"><img alt="SB*needs low angst books*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519590720p2/8385892.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="SB*needs low angst books*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SB*needs low angst books*" href="/user/show/8385892-sb-needs-low-angst-books">SB*needs low angst books*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488499730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18162912429052885437">This was a really good story. I enjoyed the heroine Reece and the hero Brody. I got the audiobook version and I thought the narrator did a decent job telling the story.<br/><br/>Reece is a trained chef who survived a horrible attack and had many mental issues she dealt with afterward which after such an event is understandable. <br/><br/>Brody is a writer that has lived in the town after he quit a newspaper job and has become a novelist. He is blunt, a loner and observant. He doesn't coddle but does care when he le</span>
  <span id="freeText18162912429052885437" style="display:none">This was a really good story. I enjoyed the heroine Reece and the hero Brody. I got the audiobook version and I thought the narrator did a decent job telling the story.<br /><br />Reece is a trained chef who survived a horrible attack and had many mental issues she dealt with afterward which after such an event is understandable. <br /><br />Brody is a writer that has lived in the town after he quit a newspaper job and has become a novelist. He is blunt, a loner and observant. He doesn't coddle but does care when he lets someone in but isn't a super romantic type of guy but it fits the heroine. <br /><br /><br />In this story, Reece is going across country on a journey to try to keep healing and find herself again. She stops in a town called Angels Fist and her car breaks down. Her money is running low and decides on whim to take a cook position at a local diner and meets many of the townspeople including the hero, Brody. On a hike, she witnesses a murder and runs and bumps into hero Brody who she tells what she sees and they report it. <br /><br />After this happens, the townspeople find out her history and doubts of her sanity are planted in the minds of some while her she is having things happen to her that make her think so too. Brody and her boss Jodie help keep her steady thru all the rumors and things that begin happening to her. Her and Brody start trying to solve the case while they get closer and they develop a more serious relationship. <br /><br />I enjoyed watching their relationship develop and the mystery unfold. I loved Brody personally because I loved his matter a fact ways but loved that he cared. I loved Reece and loved her trying to overcome and succeeding. <br /><br />I didn't like the secondary characters Lo and Linda Gail relationship development. I really felt Linda Gail was super immature. Her comment about him being a whore was stupid especially when you want to marry him. I mean really. And her ways to get him just annoyed me. This part is what brought it down for me. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18162912429052885437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4169022217235458420"><b>*Buddy read with Blacky <3<3<3*<br/><br/>*4,5 stars*</b><br/><br/>Another great romantic suspense by Nora Roberts. I loved everything, the characters, the build up and the general plot.<br/><br/><b>The characters:</b><br/><b>Reece</b> is the only survivor of a traumatic event, she's roaming the country doing small jobs trying to find her way back to a "normal" life.   <span id="freeText4169022217235458420" style="display:none"><b>*Buddy read with Blacky &lt;3&lt;3&lt;3*<br /><br />*4,5 stars*</b><br /><br />Another great romantic suspense by Nora Roberts. I loved everything, the characters, the build up and the general plot.<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><b>Reece</b> is the only survivor of a traumatic event, she's roaming the country doing small jobs trying to find her way back to a "normal" life. Before that she was a successful chef. Because of what happened to her she's fragile, but mostly she's strong and I loved her temper tantrum. <br /><b>Brody</b> is a reclusive writer. He's snarky, borderline rude, commitment shy, but mostly he just speaks his mind and I <b>l o v e d</b> him.<br />I <b>loved</b> their conversations and how Brody always believed Reece and how despite his cantankerous nature he always stood up for her. I also loved how he reacted when Reece was having her panic attacks. <br /><br />The secondary characters were interesting too. <br /><br /><b>The build up:</b><br />Be it for the romance or the suspense, the built up has the perfect pace. Not too fast, not too slow. <br /><br /><b>The plot:</b><br />I have to admit that the killer was so obvious that I dismissed him from the beginning. Because of that, I kept guessing the whole book about his identity. <br /><br /><br /><b>"I've put you to a lot of trouble today," she began.<br />"Damn right you have.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347596977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11849998002180316443"><b>3 Stars!</b> Not bad, but after listening to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716613.The_Witness' title='The Witness by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Witness</a> and being blown away by the narrator, plot and characters, this one didn't quite measure up. It took me a while to get used to the "voice" that was narrating this story, and I wonder if I had "read" the book, would I have enjoyed it more...I'm not sure. <br/><br/>The plot was intriguing, but at mid-point I guessed who the killer was. Nora Roberts tried so hard to direct your attention to another character and make it obvious it was him, that it was obvi</span>
  <span id="freeText11849998002180316443" style="display:none"><b>3 Stars!</b> Not bad, but after listening to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716613.The_Witness" title="The Witness by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witness</a> and being blown away by the narrator, plot and characters, this one didn't quite measure up. It took me a while to get used to the "voice" that was narrating this story, and I wonder if I had "read" the book, would I have enjoyed it more...I'm not sure. <br /><br />The plot was intriguing, but at mid-point I guessed who the killer was. Nora Roberts tried so hard to direct your attention to another character and make it obvious it was him, that it was obvious it was not...does that make any sense?? I also had issue with how mean and blunt everyone was towards Reece, the woman who believed she witnessed a murder and was the survivor of a VERY traumatic event. I know they were doing the "tough love" thing with her, but it came off nasty and not at all loving. Brody, her love interest got better over time, but initially I didn't care for him at all. And Joanie, her know-it-all boss...blech!!! I couldn't stand her!! Again, was it the "voice"? All I could picture was this wrinkled old woman with cigarette in her hand, rasping out commands and insults at Reece! This contradicted her character description as a business savvy, BEAUTIFUL woman!! Not the way I saw it, or rather heard it! <br /><br />Not my favorite read, but not horrible either. I like Nora Roberts style, love the audiobook format and look forward to reading and listening to more of her books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11849998002180316443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=not-for-the-sensitive">not-for-the-sensitive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=favorite-2011-reads">favorite-2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167434008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18232894680529970401">I never expected much from Nora Roberts. After I was <s>coerced</s> convinced to try one by a friend, I picked up the unremarkable <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40530.Time_and_Again__Time_Travel___1_2_' title='Time and Again (Time Travel, #1-2) by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Time and Again</a> and was, shall we say, less than impressed. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/491040.Cordina_s_Crown_Jewel__Cordina___4___Silhouette_Special_Edition__1448_' title='Cordina's Crown Jewel (Cordina, #4) (Silhouette Special Edition #1448) by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cordina's Crown Jewel (Cordina, #4)</a> was an improvement; <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26046.Morrigan_s_Cross__Circle_Trilogy___1_' title='Morrigan's Cross (Circle Trilogy, #1) by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Morrigan's Cross</a> was a misery. After four books, I had only a slightly better understanding of why people liked them so much. I never expected to give one of her novels five stars.<br/><br/>Well, Angels Fall deserved every one of them. Everything I disliked about the oth</span>
  <span id="freeText18232894680529970401" style="display:none">I never expected much from Nora Roberts. After I was <s>coerced</s> convinced to try one by a friend, I picked up the unremarkable <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40530.Time_and_Again__Time_Travel___1_2_" title="Time and Again (Time Travel, #1-2) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Time and Again</a> and was, shall we say, less than impressed. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/491040.Cordina_s_Crown_Jewel__Cordina___4___Silhouette_Special_Edition__1448_" title="Cordina's Crown Jewel (Cordina, #4) (Silhouette Special Edition #1448) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Cordina's Crown Jewel (Cordina, #4)</a> was an improvement; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26046.Morrigan_s_Cross__Circle_Trilogy___1_" title="Morrigan's Cross (Circle Trilogy, #1) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Morrigan's Cross</a> was a misery. After four books, I had only a slightly better understanding of why people liked them so much. I never expected to give one of her novels five stars.<br /><br />Well, Angels Fall deserved every one of them. Everything I disliked about the other books was better in this one. The asshole heroes of Time and Again can't hold a candle to smart, reclusive, caring Brody. Neither can the heroines match talented, strong, clever Reece. And the chemistry between them - well. Not long ago, the fellows at <i>Writing Excuses</i> did an episode on romance with a guest author, and she told them that a good couple needed to complete each other. Reece and Brody absolutely do. But the best part? They're not cheesy. Their relationship, their dialogue, everything feels completely natural.<br /><br />I'll get back to Reece and Brody in a moment, because I want to talk about the plot. <i>Damn</i>, that was a fun mystery! I admit, I guessed wrong - even though I should have known better. I guessed wrong and the real killer was, to quote Writing Excuses again, "surprising but inevitable". The climax was tense and awesome, and the buildup was genuinely scary. I thought Reece was going crazy. I really did. And that freaked me out a bit, but mostly just added wonderful to the tension.<br /><br />And speaking of wonderful... the writing in this book just sparkled. I actually laughed, four or five times even! Lines like this:<br />"Well, I'd have more zing with George Clooney and Harrison Ford in a threesome, but neither of us are going to get that wish."<br />How could anyone not laugh at that?<br /><br />I was worried, as a Westerner, that the characters in this book wouldn't sound like they belonged in Wyoming. Well, they absolutely do. My favorite was Joanie, the sharp-tongued entrepreneur who becomes Reece's boss, but all the rest of the characters were spot-on too. The little details, even - at one point Roberts mentions a beer called Buttface Amber, and she didn't make that up. You can really get it out here. It was a nice little touch.<br /><br />Okay, back to Reece and Brody.<br />God, Brody. He couldn't have been any hotter unless he was a wizard. (No one knocks Numair off the Throne of Hotness; sorry.) I mean, damn. First off, he's an author, which probably appeals to most female readers right away. Second, while he at first seems cantankerous and possibly rude, he's a softie at heart - as he aptly demonstrated with his patience and his faith in Reece. Third, and perhaps most important, he doesn't think with his libido. When Reece asks him to stop, he stops; and unlike other Roberts heroes, he doesn't think of her sexually from the moment they meet. In fact, mostly when he thinks of Reece he thinks of her strength and her passion for her work. Watching him fall in love with her is just beautiful.<br /><br />As for Reece herself, well... I was worried she'd be a doormat, especially since she comes with some heavy emotional baggage. My worries were wholly unfounded. Reece is a pistol! She is, as Brody works to convince her, astonishingly strong. She is also very responsible and mature. Case in point:<br />"What do you want, Reece?"<br />"To push rewind, I guess. But since I can't, to deal with the consequences."<br />This girl is <u>awesome</u>.<br />She really needed Brody, but not in an annoying sappy way - she needed someone who would believe in her, not pity her, treat her like an ordinary person and not something fragile. She also needed someone to respect her for her strength, and Brody was both. Through letting herself get close to him, she freed herself of a fear of losing someone she loved - and though I won't spoil, that fear was replaced by kickass determination.<br /><br />Two final things:<br />If you like Coldplay, put on a big playlist of their music to listen to while reading this. It's pretty much perfect, I think, and <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=i-n75KVcGsw" rel="nofollow noopener">Yellow</a> is totally Reece and Brody's song.<br /><br />I wondered before I started this why it had recipes in the back, and now I know: it <u>will</u> make you hungry. Have a snack or a drink to hand. (I went through a bottle of water, half a bag of Goldfish, a chocolate bar, and dinner.)<br /><br /><br />Vinaya, recommend me more please?</span>
  <a data-text-id="18232894680529970401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158269957" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158269957" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158269957?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-loved">books-i-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=re-reading-times-1-million">re-reading-times-1-million</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=comparative-5-stars">comparative-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=nora-week-with-flann-and-maureen">nora-week-with-flann-and-maureen</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158269957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3630970210844020189">It seems fitting to conclude Nothing But Nora Week with my absolute favourite Nora book of all time. Why do I like Angels Fall so much? Maybe because it is inspired by my two favourite psychological thrillers, Gaslight and Rear Window. I've watched both movies a million times, but I still get that goosebump-ey feeling as the dénouement approaches. <br/><br/>Reece Gilmore lands up in the little Wyoming town of Angels Fist while she's running away from the ghosts of her past. She finds a job as a short-orde</span>
  <span id="freeText3630970210844020189" style="display:none">It seems fitting to conclude Nothing But Nora Week with my absolute favourite Nora book of all time. Why do I like Angels Fall so much? Maybe because it is inspired by my two favourite psychological thrillers, Gaslight and Rear Window. I've watched both movies a million times, but I still get that goosebump-ey feeling as the dénouement approaches. <br /><br />Reece Gilmore lands up in the little Wyoming town of Angels Fist while she's running away from the ghosts of her past. She finds a job as a short-order cook in a diner and slowly begins to settle down when she becomes a witness to a murder in a remote spot. Reece's claim regarding the murder are dismissed by the town sheriff when he can find no evidence of such an attack taking place, and her credibility is further compromised by her troubled emotional state. Her only firm ally is reclusive writer Brody, whom she teams up with to prove that she is not deranged, and that a murder really DID take place as claimed. <br /><br />Angels Fall was, for me, a very different book from the run-of-the-mill romantic suspense/thrillers I've read so far. Reece is a great character, troubled, disturbed and clinging onto sanity by a thread. The plot is fast-paced and thrilling. The mind-games that the murderer plays with Reece are chilling and satisfyingly convoluted. And the final dénouement is everything a whodunnit fan could ask for. <br /><br />All-in-all, this is a book that is definitely worth reading, for all fans of romantic suspense. To be honest, I kind of skipped over the romance part quite a bit because I was so caught up in the story, but for the not-so-jaded, the romance between Brody and Reece is definitely sigh-inducing. Must. Read. <br /><br />On a side note, I'm told the TV movie of this book is crappy, so you might want to avoid that...<br /><br /><b>Nothing But Nora Week, Book 7</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3630970210844020189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163326034" />
    <a title="Lisa Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay"><img alt="Lisa Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534570690p2/2459470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163326034?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Kay" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay">Lisa Kay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781441810717" href="/book/show/7672117-angels-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=has-a-movie">has-a-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-n">authors-n</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=vocation-chef">vocation-chef</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-r">authors-r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=genre-romance-suspense">genre-romance-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=m-library-sj-audio-oda">m-library-sj-audio-oda</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=zzcover-teal-turquoise">zzcover-teal-turquoise</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163326034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13974168764673042265"><a href='http://media.photobucket.com/image/yellowstone%20waterfall/flyingblueheron/Yellowstone/Picture029.jpg?o=18' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348881i/703008._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Five full stars! ★★★★★ I love books about chefs! Whether they are romances or mysteries; I just love the culinary theme (guess this explains my fascination with the Food Network!). Put the three together, and Wow! I’ve never been a huge <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts' title='Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts</a> fan (though I do like her writing as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb' title='J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.D. Robb</a>); nevertheless, I’ve picked up one or two of her books over the years and enjoyed them.<br/><br/>However, I’ve always liked Heather Locklear (I swear my sister-in-law could be her twin). Ms. Locklear starred i</span>
  <span id="freeText13974168764673042265" style="display:none"><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/yellowstone%20waterfall/flyingblueheron/Yellowstone/Picture029.jpg?o=18" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348881i/703008._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Five full stars! ★★★★★ I love books about chefs! Whether they are romances or mysteries; I just love the culinary theme (guess this explains my fascination with the Food Network!). Put the three together, and Wow! I’ve never been a huge <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" title="Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts</a> fan (though I do like her writing as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb" title="J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">J.D. Robb</a>); nevertheless, I’ve picked up one or two of her books over the years and enjoyed them.<br><br>However, I’ve always liked Heather Locklear (I swear my sister-in-law could be her twin). Ms. Locklear starred in the wonderful 2007 “made-for-TV-movie” adaptation of Ms. Roberts’ <i>Angels Fall</i> and I really relished it. When I saw this volume available from my library on audio download, I went for it. I am glad I did! Wow! It was even better than the movie (isn’t the book <i>
  <b>always</b>
</i> better?)! <br><br>Well worth the read – or listen!<br><br>P.S. Almost forgot: Joyce Bean does an excellent job of narrating the audiobook!<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7672117.Angels_Fall" title="Angels Fall by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> <br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/angels%20fall/yosuaaa/AngelsFall.jpg?o=124" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer9194280843171113309">3.5 stars. Enjoyable.<br/><br/>I read the physical book several years ago and thought it was good - 4 ½ stars. But I changed my mind when I recently listened to the audiobook. The middle dragged too much. Maybe because I knew the ending and who the bad guy was, but I was tired of Reese being oblivious to all the things being done to her by the bad guy - trying to make her lose her mind. Although she did some interesting things, too much time was spent with her being a helpless victim.<br/><br/>The story is about a </span>
  <span id="freeText9194280843171113309" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Enjoyable.<br /><br />I read the physical book several years ago and thought it was good - 4 ½ stars. But I changed my mind when I recently listened to the audiobook. The middle dragged too much. Maybe because I knew the ending and who the bad guy was, but I was tired of Reese being oblivious to all the things being done to her by the bad guy - trying to make her lose her mind. Although she did some interesting things, too much time was spent with her being a helpless victim.<br /><br />The story is about a talented woman chef who was the only survivor of a gunshot massacre. She moves away, is in the process of healing, and witnesses another murder. It’s a good murder mystery. The story also has an interesting romance developing between the chef and a writer who helps her. I enjoyed reading about these two characters. I also enjoyed a supporting character, Joanie, owner of the diner. There were some good lines. I'm extracting parts of them here briefly, but they are better within the context of the story. Page 211, after he said her eyes looked tired, she thought "He would always be brutally honest with her. Tough as it might be on the ego, it was better than platitudes and soft lies." Page 266 "a man puts his hands around a woman's throat once, he could do it again." Page 279 "what selfishness you have seems awfully healthy from where I stand."<br /><br />AUDIOBOOK NARRATOR:<br />Joyce Bean was fine, although her voice for men was a little weird.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 3rd person. Swearing language: strong but rarely used. Sexual language: mild. Number of sex scenes: four. Setting: current day Wyoming. Copyright: 2006. Genre: romantic mystery.</span>

<div id="review_824012020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/824012020" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/824012020?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=romance-contemp">romance-contemp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer824012020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13257167571891235779">3.75 stars. From the perspective of a murder mystery, the plot was fairly gripping, but the killer was a bit obvious, and remained my most constant suspect throughout the book, even though I considered others, since it seemed too obvious. <br/><br/>I felt for heroine Reece, and all the harrowing terror she had been through in Boston, and now murder and malice here in Angels Fall, Wyoming, at the foot of the Grand Tetons. My heart went out to her when the killer tried to drive her loco. Well done!<br/><br/>Romance? </span>
  <span id="freeText13257167571891235779" style="display:none">3.75 stars. From the perspective of a murder mystery, the plot was fairly gripping, but the killer was a bit obvious, and remained my most constant suspect throughout the book, even though I considered others, since it seemed too obvious. <br /><br />I felt for heroine Reece, and all the harrowing terror she had been through in Boston, and now murder and malice here in Angels Fall, Wyoming, at the foot of the Grand Tetons. My heart went out to her when the killer tried to drive her loco. Well done!<br /><br />Romance? Well, I liked the couple, Reece and Brody, and how they rolled. No rainbows, hearts, or starry-eyed sparkles -- this romance is fairly unemotional -- but Brody the grouch grew on me. I liked how he slowly began to reveal his soft spot for Reece. I liked him for believing in her when few others would, and for being so protective. <br /><br />Good secondary characters, especially Joanie, the restaurant owner.<br /><br />Clever parallel between the heroine of the murder mystery Brody was writing and the actual heroine, Reece.<br /><br />Good descriptions of the Tetons. I have been there, and Roberts' depictions brought all that grandeur, serenity, and majesty right back.<br /><br />It needed a longer ending. I wanted to know how the townspeople reacted.<br /><br />Audio narration by Joyce Bean was fine. Quite good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13257167571891235779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola O." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola O." href="/user/show/165632-nicola-o">Nicola O.</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17188654752344573908">I'm a bit undecided about a 3 vs. 4 for this one. I have a certain devotion to Nora Roberts that some might find irrational, but generally I find her characters interesting & distinguishable, and their conflict/relationships satisfying. My 3.5 rating rationale would go something like this: <br/><br/>*Never saw the 'whodunit' coming-- that's good!--4 stars!<br/>*Plot holes that would enable the culprit to do what was done-- uh, 3 stars.<br/><br/>In the end, I'm giving it 4 because I like NR. If you are picky about myster</span>
  <span id="freeText17188654752344573908" style="display:none">I'm a bit undecided about a 3 vs. 4 for this one. I have a certain devotion to Nora Roberts that some might find irrational, but generally I find her characters interesting &amp; distinguishable, and their conflict/relationships satisfying. My 3.5 rating rationale would go something like this: <br /><br />*Never saw the 'whodunit' coming-- that's good!--4 stars!<br />*Plot holes that would enable the culprit to do what was done-- uh, 3 stars.<br /><br />In the end, I'm giving it 4 because I like NR. If you are picky about mystery plotting, you may find it frustrating. If you're in it for the characters, it's really good. I especially like the sort of grouchy Lou Grant voice of the hero.<br /></span>

<div id="review_763607480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/763607480" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/763607480?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer763607480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2931092851011148133">This book was a light, but entertaining mystery/romance and about what you'd expect from Nora Roberts--i.e. well-written, with interesting characters, and a firm sense of place and people.<br/><br/>I really like Reece as someone recovering from a truly awful, traumatic experience. She's been nomadic for a while and settles in a small Wyoming town when her car breaks down there. It isn't long before she finds herself integrating into the town, making friends, and setting down the beginnings of roots.<br/><br/>I'm le</span>
  <span id="freeText2931092851011148133" style="display:none">This book was a light, but entertaining mystery/romance and about what you'd expect from Nora Roberts--i.e. well-written, with interesting characters, and a firm sense of place and people.<br /><br />I really like Reece as someone recovering from a truly awful, traumatic experience. She's been nomadic for a while and settles in a small Wyoming town when her car breaks down there. It isn't long before she finds herself integrating into the town, making friends, and setting down the beginnings of roots.<br /><br />I'm less sanguine with the leading man, Brody. He's a bit caustic, in an alpha male, take-charge kind of way. He fights falling for Reece a little too assiduously and seems randomly emotionally immature. It ended up working, I guess, and I buy their eventual HEA, but with the occasional needlessly exasperating moment.<br /><br />The mystery of the novel was a bit awkward, too. I guessed the real culprit relatively early, though there's a real paucity of information through most of the book so it's never possible to be sure. By about the three-quarters mark, I was ready for that part to be done--or at least show some progress. The nature of the mystery meant that once any details came out it wouldn't take long for the rest to fall into place, though, so Roberts really had no choice but to string it out a while. As I said... awkward...<br /><br />In the end, this was a good romance with a relationship that worked, if rocky in places. Not my favorite Nora Roberts, but certainly worth the time.<br /><br /><strong>A note about steamy</strong>: On the light side for Roberts. One full-on explicit sex scene, on the short side, and a handful of playful interludes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2931092851011148133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer40653210" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15629858545855693374">Turned out that, despite all the various <a href='http://annathepiper.livejournal.com/696943.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts recommendations</a> folks kindly gave me, the first non-J.D. Robb of hers that I read was <i>Angels Fall</i>, her latest paperback. Turned out to be pretty good, overall. A talented young chef, after being the only survivor of a violent crime back East, travels across the country and winds up in a small town in the mountains--where she is the only witness to a murder. Only did she really see what she thought she did? Most of the town is dubious, except </span>
  <span id="freeText15629858545855693374" style="display:none">Turned out that, despite all the various <a href="http://annathepiper.livejournal.com/696943.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts recommendations</a> folks kindly gave me, the first non-J.D. Robb of hers that I read was <i>Angels Fall</i>, her latest paperback. Turned out to be pretty good, overall. A talented young chef, after being the only survivor of a violent crime back East, travels across the country and winds up in a small town in the mountains--where she is the only witness to a murder. Only did she really see what she thought she did? Most of the town is dubious, except for the writer who's taken a shine to her and believes she's telling the truth.<br /><br />I already know Roberts' writing from the In Death series, of course, but this novel felt a bit meatier than most of those books--possibly because there was only the one book to spend on developing these characters. And I'll say this for ol' Nora: she actually surprised me for who turned out to be the murderer. I spent most of the book thinking it was somebody else entirely. Also, thumbs up for the heroine and hero being refreshingly equal in their growing attraction, and the heroine being <i>very</i> honest about laying down her boundaries and when she's ready to cross them, and the hero respecting that quite a bit. The sex scenes were also familiar in style from the J.D. Robbs, and I do like Nora's style--she peppers her novels with several very small sex scenes and yet manages to make the flavor of each distinctive.<br /><br />Thinking about it, I can't come up with a single beef I have with this book. So sure, let's say four stars. ^_^</span>
  <a data-text-id="15629858545855693374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText17221169586048833911" style="display:none">Rating 2.5- 3 stars.<br /><br />Hmm the whole small town which should have come across as quaint and wholesome didn't...instead it came off across as a small town with a very idyllic view but extremely unempathetic people. I really don't understand why anyone would prefer to live there but Reece and Brody did clearly. <br /><br />The only person I liked was Reece. <span id="freeTextContainer6435788317724435314">3,5 <br/><br/>After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114203.Birthright' title='Birthright by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Birthright</a>, this book fell far short of expectations. Reece Gilmore was an interesting character, but became more interesting after witnessing the murder and having her sanity put into question by almost everyone, given her traumatic past. Unfortunately, I don’t think she was given much depth. Same goes for Brody. I didn’t really like the guy, and e</span>
  <span id="freeText6435788317724435314" style="display:none">3,5 <br /><br />After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114203.Birthright" title="Birthright by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Birthright</a>, this book fell far short of expectations. I really liked all the elements of the story, especially the spectacular landscape. Loved the interaction between the townspeople. Reece Gilmore was an interesting character, but became more interesting after witnessing the murder and having her sanity put into question by almost everyone, given her traumatic past. Unfortunately, I don’t think she was given much depth. Same goes for Brody. I didn’t really like the guy, and even though he redeemed himself a bit by the end, I’m still not a fan; I thought the dialogues were feeble in comparison to other books. The story had everything, but at the same time seemed sparse. The last <i>gotcha! </i> part was good but the private investigation took a little too much. Yet, I didn’t see that coming (<i>damn</i>, I knew there was something about that kid and the dog playing in the lake). My money was on Doctor Wallace. Lo proved to be too dumb to be a killer. Needless to say, I was way off. I enjoyed the story, worth a few good hours of entertainment. The end, though, was cut too short. <br /><br />A small note on translation. <br />In chapter 3, page 38, there’s the following sentence:<br /><br />– Sim, senhora. Ah, e só para <b>limpar o ambiente</b>, o seu filho é encantador, mas eu dormi sozinha ontem à noite.<br /><br />It’s the Portuguese translation of the original English:<br /><br />“Yes, ma'am. Oh, and just to <b>clear the air</b>," she added as she rounded the counter for an apron, "your son's very charming, but I slept alone last night." <br /><br />Notice the expressions in bold, it jumped right at me when I first read it, and I actually laughed, because the translator took it literally, and she didn’t even translate the whole sentence. In this context “clear the air” means resolving a situation or making things straight. I think “só para esclarecer” instead of “limpar o ambiente” would be more accurate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6435788317724435314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="D.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3754562-d-r"><img alt="D.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442894445p2/3754562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/712386499?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="D.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="D.R." href="/user/show/3754562-d-r">D.R.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer712386499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14255271421450705842">Giving this a 4 star cause I am rereading it. That's my cut off for 4 stars. I don't reread a lot of books. I just can't most times. Even if the book was good or even okay. There has to be something more to make me want to crack it open again. My brain works weird that way. I dunno. Sometimes I can remember scenes from books from years and years ago and rereading a book makes me unhappy. Othertimes, I can't wait for enough time to pass for me to be able to open it back up. Angels Fall is a book </span>
  <span id="freeText14255271421450705842" style="display:none">Giving this a 4 star cause I am rereading it. That's my cut off for 4 stars. I don't reread a lot of books. I just can't most times. Even if the book was good or even okay. There has to be something more to make me want to crack it open again. My brain works weird that way. I dunno. Sometimes I can remember scenes from books from years and years ago and rereading a book makes me unhappy. Othertimes, I can't wait for enough time to pass for me to be able to open it back up. Angels Fall is a book I can't wait for enough time to pass. Seriously good book. <br /><br />Yeah, it's one of her best so far and I have probably read almost all her stuff from way back. This one and Witness, I just can't get out of my head. I don't think it is one thing in the book- not the characters, not the setting, not the storyline. It's a combo of all those things that turns a tale into a fab story. <br /><br />Some books touch others that I think are meh, I can take it or leave it. And I know the reverse is true for those same others for books that make my mind happy. So whatever it is about this book... it made me chomp at the bit for enough to pass so I could read it again. <br /><br />One thing I gotta say. I'm usually not a big fan of broken heroines. Not broken like the female lead in this book. And I'm not usually a fan of broody asshole heroes. At least not like this one. But, they worked in this story and they worked well. Well enough that I overlooked my usual disdain for such obvious character flaws that normally become a plot device in and of themselves. The mystery and suspense worked as well. And they were melded in such a way that the overall story- AWESOME. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14255271421450705842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7685408040639464179">Wow. I was on a pretty good roll there for a bit. "No more TV!" I said. "I'll read instead!" I was finishing books at a respectable pace for a graduate student! Then school ended and you'd think I would be reading up a storm. Instead I got the world's cutest, smartest puppy and I have been working on a fluff book, a Nora Roberts re-read for THREE WEEKS. How embarrassing is that? I used to read in the morning during breakfast and at night before bed. Now on the rare occasions I am sitting down wi</span>
  <span id="freeText7685408040639464179" style="display:none">Wow. I was on a pretty good roll there for a bit. "No more TV!" I said. "I'll read instead!" I was finishing books at a respectable pace for a graduate student! Then school ended and you'd think I would be reading up a storm. Instead I got the world's cutest, smartest puppy and I have been working on a fluff book, a Nora Roberts re-read for THREE WEEKS. How embarrassing is that? I used to read in the morning during breakfast and at night before bed. Now on the rare occasions I am sitting down with tea, I am usually watching the puppy play in his pen. Sigh. But I finally finished Angels Fall (which, like I said, is a re-read for me). This is the book that The Witness reminded me of, and it's so much better than The Witness that I felt compelled to revisit it. Like The Witness, it's the story of a woman who has suffered severe emotional and psychological trauma making a life for herself and falling in love. The protagonist is much more likable, and it's set in Wyoming, which is kind of cool to read about. The only thing I can't stand about this book is the protagonist suffers from what I guess is PTSD--she constantly has to check her locks, put barriers in front of her doors--but does she get a dog? No. Moron.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline J" href="/user/show/2999717-jacqueline-j">Jacqueline J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2999717-jacqueline-j?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2999717-jacqueline-j?shelf=from-the-library">from-the-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81253381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16264074169583440911">Nora Roberts is usually a slightly above middle of the road read for me. This one she hit out of the park. Reece is the only survivor of a shooting spree in Boston. At her new place in Wyoming she witnesses a murder but because of her history of a breakdown after the first shooting no one believes her.<br/><br/>Characterization is wonderful. Reece grows over the course of the book. She starts out fragile and very damaged and grows stronger in what she is mentally able to accomplish and she doesn't give up</span>
  <span id="freeText16264074169583440911" style="display:none">Nora Roberts is usually a slightly above middle of the road read for me. This one she hit out of the park. Reece is the only survivor of a shooting spree in Boston. At her new place in Wyoming she witnesses a murder but because of her history of a breakdown after the first shooting no one believes her.<br /><br />Characterization is wonderful. Reece grows over the course of the book. She starts out fragile and very damaged and grows stronger in what she is mentally able to accomplish and she doesn't give up on trying to find the murder that only she saw. The hero, Brody, was not at all a cookie cutter hero. He is a mystery writer and is surly and sarcastic and doesn't fall all over her trying to baby her. He does believe her though and learns to love her.<br /><br />There are several very interesting secondary characters and enough red herrings to keep me guessing as to the murderer for much longer than normal in this sort of book.<br /><br />The mystery and romance were blended and balanced perfectly in this one. Not an edge of your seat thriller but a more character driven book.<br /><br />Really sterling writing and just perfect reading for a long Sunday afternoon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16264074169583440911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011635540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13617471419304116323">4 stars - 2015<br/><br/><br/>3.5 STARS - 2007 <br/><br/>"Reece Gilmore has come a long way to see the stunning view below her. As the sole survivor of a brutal crime back East, she has been on the run, desperately fighting the nightmares and panic attacks that haunt her. Reece settles in Angel's Fist, Wyoming-temporarily, at least-and takes a job at a local diner. And now she's hiked this mountain all by herself. It was glorious, she thought, as she peered through her binoculars at the Snake River churning below.<br/><br/>Then Re</span>
  <span id="freeText13617471419304116323" style="display:none">4 stars - 2015<br /><br /><br />3.5 STARS - 2007 <br /><br />"Reece Gilmore has come a long way to see the stunning view below her. As the sole survivor of a brutal crime back East, she has been on the run, desperately fighting the nightmares and panic attacks that haunt her. Reece settles in Angel's Fist, Wyoming-temporarily, at least-and takes a job at a local diner. And now she's hiked this mountain all by herself. It was glorious, she thought, as she peered through her binoculars at the Snake River churning below.<br /><br />Then Reece saw the man and woman on the opposite bank. Arguing. Fighting. And suddenly, the man was on top of the woman, his hands around her throat . . .<br /><br />Enjoying a moment of solitude a bit farther down the trail is a gruff loner named Brody. But by the time Reece reaches him and brings him to the scene, the pair has vanished. When authorities comb the area where she saw the attack, they find nothing. No signs of struggle. No freshly turned earth. Not even a tire track.<br /><br />And no one in Angel's Fist seems to believe her. After all, she's a newcomer in town, with a reputation for being jumpy and jittery-maybe even a little fragile. Maybe it's time to run again, to move on . . .<br /><br />Reece Gilmore knows there's a killer in Angel's Fist, even if Brody, despite his seeming impatience and desire to keep her at arm's length, is the only one willing to believe her. When a series of menacing events makes it clear that someone wants her out of the way, Reece must put her trust in Brody-and herself-to find out if there is a killer in Angel's Fist before it's too late." (From Amazon)<br /><br />I really enjoyed this novel. I was able to read this novel cover to cover in one sitting. I will read more of Roberts novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13617471419304116323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1183731901?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CaroB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CaroB" href="/user/show/4581712-carob">CaroB</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780786580439" href="/book/show/7468742-angels-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=drama-angst">drama-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=intrigue-mystery-suspense">intrigue-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=would-reread">would-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4581712-carob?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183731901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6738037851560884162">I had originally read this back in 2011, but have to admit to having forgotten who the villain was in this when I started the re-read. <br/>As for the protagonists, I absolutely loved Brody's surliness, his "no bullshit" attitude with a heart of gold. It's true that if I were to actually meet someone like him in real life, I probably would not give him the time of day after decided he was arrogant and rude, but Nora Roberts manages to make it understandable how he was exactly what Reece needed in her</span>
  <span id="freeText6738037851560884162" style="display:none">I had originally read this back in 2011, but have to admit to having forgotten who the villain was in this when I started the re-read. <br />As for the protagonists, I absolutely loved Brody's surliness, his "no bullshit" attitude with a heart of gold. It's true that if I were to actually meet someone like him in real life, I probably would not give him the time of day after decided he was arrogant and rude, but Nora Roberts manages to make it understandable how he was exactly what Reece needed in her life when she came to Angels' Fist. I've tried a couple of times in the last couple of year to read another standalone (Whiskey Beach) by Nora Roberts, but just can't get into it and was wondering if I had maybe gone "off" her writing style. Great to affirm with this read that that's not the case. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6738037851560884162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/Mf+gADcfm7pjFak4gWpBFbzkH6t2OJk9EYMoMeSZpsmPO1eeodxIPoqiaGXiUYlf71QWZxppeNT1pDVVIRDrw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A8apt+JoaCqOuo/WPADutx96VbSpnu5VmFsLfpO2G6zZPbppmDNnZJ0cUNNJjAGWNjSVk5gvqdI/y5cLAKA+mA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer6571612076737691791">Nora Roberts is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of more than 200 novels, including Hideaway, Under Currents, Come Sundown and coming in November 2020 -- The Awakening -- the first book in The Dragon Heart Legacy. She is also the author of the futuristic suspense In Death series written under the pen name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb' title='J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.D. Robb</a>. There are more than 500 million copies of her books in print.</span>
